<hr class="hrule"><br>
<p class="otherpara">The electrochemical kinetics in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode during the cycling process has been assessed <span class="italic">via</span> recording CV plots at various scan rates (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5a</a>). With scan rate increase, the current intensity is enhanced and there is a slight variation in the peak positions suggesting that diffusion is not the only mechanism driving the electrochemical reaction. The relation between scan rate (<span class="italic"></span>) and current (<span class="italic">i</span>) varies as follows:</p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn6">
<span id="eqn6">log<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]"><span class="italic">i</span> = <span class="italic">b</span><img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">log<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]"><span class="italic"></span> + log<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]"><span class="italic">a</span></span>
</span></td><td class="rightEqn">(6)</td></tr></tbody></table><p></p>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2022/RA/d2ra02014a/d2ra02014a-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2ra02014a-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2022/RA/d2ra02014a/d2ra02014a-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">(a) CV curves of 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite for SIBs at scan rates ranging from 0.1 to 1 mV s <small><sup>1</sup></small>; (b) log(<span class="italic">i</span>) <span class="italic">versus</span> log(<span class="italic"></span>) plots; (c) contribution ratio of capacities at different scan rates.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">The value of <span class="italic">b</span> varies between 0.5 and 1 with <span class="italic">b</span> = 0.5 denoting diffusion controlled and <span class="italic">b</span> = 1 indicating capacitive process.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit12"><sup><span class="sup_ref">12</span></sup></a> The <span class="italic">b</span> values obtained from the slope of the log(<span class="italic">i</span>) and log(<span class="italic"></span>) plots are found to be 0.62, 0.54, 0.67 and 0.73 for peaks 1, 2, 3 and 4, respectively, which indicates both diffusion and capacitive contribution in the electrochemical process (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5b</a>). The capacitive contribution results in the improved rate capability exhibited by the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode whereas the dominant diffusion contribution yields higher specific capacity to it.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50</span></sup></a> The current contribution by the diffusion and capacitive process at any scan rate (<span class="italic"></span>) is given by the following equation:</p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn7">
<span id="eqn7"><span class="italic">i</span> = <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>1</sub></small><span class="italic"></span> + <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>2</sub></small><span class="italic"></span><small><sup>1/2</sup></small></span>
</span></td><td class="rightEqn">(7)</td></tr></tbody></table>where <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>1</sub></small> and <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>2</sub></small> are adjustable constants, <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>1</sub></small><span class="italic"></span> is the capacitive current contribution and <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>2</sub></small><span class="italic"></span><small><sup>1/2</sup></small> is the current contribution from the diffusion-controlled process. The capacitive contribution in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode increases from 15% to 36% with increase in scan rate from 0.1 to 1.0 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small> as evident from the histogram plot shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5c</a>. The decrease in size of CuS nanoparticles in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite leads to a reduction in the diffusion path length of the ions and the increase in surface area facilitates non-insertion type capacitive charge storage in the material.<p></p>
<p class="otherpara">The actual process of sodium storage in the composite has been explored by <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XPS studies. The high resolution Cu2p and S2p XPS spectra was recorded for CuS and 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite cells at various potentials (1 V, 0.1 V, 2.7 V) during the first discharge and charge process (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6ad</a>). Compared to the before cycling plot, the Cu2p spectrum at 1.0 V discharge exhibits a broad weak satellite peak at 944 eV indicating the existence of Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small> in the sample (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6a</a>). The Cu2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and Cu2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> peaks also bifurcate confirming presence of both Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> and Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small>. On further discharge up to 0.1 V, the satellite peak disappears and the Cu2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and Cu2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> peaks observed at 932.9 and 953.3 eV, respectively, is due to the formation of Cu(0). Charging up to 2.7 V again shows a satellite peak at 944.5 eV and the Cu2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and Cu2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> peaks indicate presence of both Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> and Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small>. More clarity regarding the underlying process is obtained from the S2p XPS spectra (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6b</a>). The broad peak at 169.2 eV seen in all the post-mortem analysis spectra is due to presence of sulfate which arises due to oxidation of the Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S formed during the conversion reaction.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51</span></sup></a> Compared to the before cycling spectrum, on discharge up to 1.0 V, the broad peak in the region between 161164 eV has been ascribed to the formation of polysulfides Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub><span class="italic">n</span></sub></small> where <span class="italic">n</span> values can range from 2 to 8.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42</span></sup></a> On further discharge to 0.1 V, the peaks seen at 161.7 eV and 162.6 eV are due to Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S and lower polysulfides, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42</span></sup></a> When charged to 2.7 V, the distinct peaks at 162.0 and 162.9 eV pertains to S2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and S2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51</span></sup></a> The broad tail of the peak up to 164 eV persists which indicates that the presence of polysulfides cannot be ruled out. At state of full discharge and charge, the small peak at 168 eV indicates the presence of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S in the sample.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42</span></sup></a> In case of the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode, the fitted high resolution Cu2p XPS spectrum before cycling shows peaks pertaining to Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> and Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small>, the latter being ascribed to surface oxidation (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6c</a>). On discharge to 1.0 V, the bifurcation of the peak pertaining to Cu2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> gets more pronounced while that of Cu2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> gets broader. Further discharge up to 0.1 V shows presence of Cu2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and Cu2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> peaks at 931.4 eV and 951.8 eV, respectively, which is on the lower binding energy side compared to that observed for the material before cycling and pertains to formation of Cu(0). Though the satellite peak at 944 eV is not seen, the fitted spectra shows presence of very low intensity peaks at 932.7 eV and 953.2 eV, which might be originating from some residual Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> or Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small> present in the electrode. Charging of the electrode to 2.7 V results in the formation of predominantly Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> with the Cu2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and Cu2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> peaks at 932.1 eV and 952.1 eV, respectively. On comparing <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6a and c</a>, it can be inferred, that at state of full discharge at 0.1 V, the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode has better conversion of Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> to Cu(0) compared to the pristine CuS electrode. Similar to the pristine CuS electrode, the post mortem S2p XPS spectra of the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite exhibits a broad peak at 169.2 eV indicating the presence of sulfate due to the oxidation of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S formed in the electrode during the discharge/charge process (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6d</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51</span></sup></a> Formation of polysulfide (Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub><span class="italic">n</span></sub></small> with <span class="italic">n</span> = 2 to 8) is indicated due to the presence of broad peaks in the 161164 eV range when the electrode is discharged at 1.0 V.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit41"><sup><span class="sup_ref">41</span></sup></a> Full discharge of the electrode at 0.1 V exhibit peaks at 161.7 and 162.5 eV pertaining to Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S and lower polysulfides, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit52"><sup><span class="sup_ref">52</span></sup></a> On charging to 2.7 V, binding energy peaks pertaining to presence of sulfide is clearly discernible along with broad peak at 169.2 eV indicating presence of sulfate group. However, the Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S peak at 168 eV is very weak and the main peak of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S at 161.7 eV merges with the 2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> S<small><sup>2</sup></small> peaks at 161.4 eV. The other peak at 162.5 eV correspond to S2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> of S<small><sup>2</sup></small>. The broad tail peak at 163 to 164 eV pertaining to polysulfides seen in the charged pristine CuS electrode is less conspicuous in the composite electrode. This indicates that in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite, the g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> matrix helps in reducing the polysulfide leaching and similar observation has been reported in case of g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> reinforced LiS batteries.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit53"><sup><span class="sup_ref">53</span></sup></a></p>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2022/RA/d2ra02014a/d2ra02014a-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2ra02014a-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2022/RA/d2ra02014a/d2ra02014a-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title"><span class="italic">Ex situ</span> high resolution (a) Cu2p; (b) S2p XPS of CuS electrode; (c) Cu2p; (d) S2p XPS of 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode at as prepared, discharge at 1.0 V, discharge at 0.1 V and charge at 2.7 V state.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">From the above <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XPS data, certain inferences can be drawn. The presence of Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small> in the post mortem samples cannot be unambiguously assigned to its formation in the electrochemical reaction process. Since the XPS experiment has been done <span class="italic">ex situ</span>, there is a possibility that partial oxidation of Cu<small><sup>+</sup></small> to Cu<small><sup>2+</sup></small> occurred during the loading of the sample. In the pristine CuS and 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite electrode, the S2p spectrum after discharge at 0.1 V, shows presence of Cu(0) metal, Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S and other polysulfides (Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub><span class="italic">n</span></sub></small>). This indicates that the discharge process can be summed up by the following reaction:<br></p><table><tbody><tr><td class="eqnText">CuS + 2Na  Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S + Cu</td></tr></tbody></table><p></p>
<p class="otherpara">However, the reaction occurs <span class="italic">via</span> intermediate steps of Na intercalation in CuS, followed by formation of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S and Cu(0). The presence of other polysulfides can be accounted for as Na reacts with the excess sulfur present in the sample as indicated by EDS and also by the S2p XPS spectra of it before cycling. On charging to 2.7 V, the S2p XPS of pristine CuS electrode indicates the presence of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S in the sample along with Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S and other polysulfides. The presence of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S indicates that only one Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S could desodiate in the electrode during charging and this contributes to the lowering of specific capacity on cycling. However, the presence of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S improves the <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> of the electrode on cycling which corroborates with the results obtained from EIS data. For the composite electrode, the S2p XPS obtained on charging to 2.7 V shows presence of sulfide groups indicating formation of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S which denotes some irreversibility in the reaction. However, the specific capacity remains high and is maintained throughout the repeated cycling and this cannot be explained if only one Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion is transported in the system. It is to be noted that the presence of g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> ensures that there is less loss of sulfur through polysulfide leaching and hence the capacity loss is minimized. To understand the origin of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S in the sample, the composite electrode was stripped off from the current collector after 1<small><sup>st</sup></small> charge and the ratio of Cu to S was analysed using EDS. The atomic ratio obtained was 1.89<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">:<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">1 and the excess copper most probably gets extracted from the Cu collector as the reaction between CuS and Cu is thermodynamically feasible.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15</span></sup></a> SEM of the stripped Cu current collector has a pitted appearance exhibiting loss of Cu from the surface (Fig. S7<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Similar observation has been reported in case of CuS electrodes synthesized by direct heating of S on copper current collector strips.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15</span></sup></a> Hence, it can be inferred that in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite, g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> helps in mitigating the volume expansion of CuS during the sodiation/desodiation cycles and also reduces the polysulfide leaching which enhance its electrochemical properties compared to other CuS composites reported in literature (Table S4<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The sulfiphilic nature of Cu leads to the formation of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit54"><sup><span class="sup_ref">54</span></sup></a> but the specific capacity is not compromised since the total amount of sulfur remains mostly unaltered in the composite electrode.</p>
<p class="otherpara">A sodium ion full cell has been assembled using NVP cathode and pre-sodiated 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> anode. The construction and electrochemical performance of the NVP cathode is discussed in supplementary section (Fig. S8<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The insertion of sodium ion in the composite anode was done to reduce the loss of sodium ions during the initial cycles which impacts the full cell performance.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit55"><sup><span class="sup_ref">55</span></sup></a> The full cell was cycled at 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> between the voltage range 0.23.0 V and the cycle performance and GDC plots are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7a and b</a>, respectively. A discharge capacity of 266 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> was obtained after a 100-cycle run and a capacity retention of 84.9% was observed compared to the first cycle.</p>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2022/RA/d2ra02014a/d2ra02014a-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2ra02014a-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2022/RA/d2ra02014a/d2ra02014a-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Cyclability and (b) GDC plots at 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> current rate for sodium ion full cell with NVP cathode and pre-sodiated 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> anode.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>

<h2 id="sect1338"><span class="a_heading">Conclusion</span></h2>
<span>The synthesis of 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite has been done <span class="italic">via</span> precipitation method using exfoliated g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> nanosheets as matrix for <span class="italic">in situ</span> dispersion of the CuS nanoparticles. The pristine CuS nanoparticles exhibits a reversible capacity of 304 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> current rate after a run of 200 cycles which improves to 478.4 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 2.0 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> current rate after 1000 cycles run in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite when used as anode in lithium ion half-cell. In sodium ion half-cell, the composite delivers a reversible capacity of 408 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 2.0 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> current rate after a run of 800 cycles which is superior to that exhibited by pristine CuS (212 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, 1.0 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, 800 cycles). The presence of pyridinic N enriched exfoliated g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> improves the Li<small><sup>+</sup></small>/Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion conductivity and the higher surface area and pore volume of the composite compared to pristine CuS improves the penetration of electrolyte in the anode. The even dispersion of CuS nanoparticles in g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> prevents agglomeration and shortens the diffusion length of the ions and also provides space for their movement during the discharge/charge process thereby reducing the detrimental effect of volume alteration associated with these conversion anodes. The formation of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S from CuS during the electrochemical reaction has been established <span class="italic">via ex situ</span> XPS studies and the reduction in reversible capacity with cycling has been accounted for in case of pristine CuS anode. However, in the 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> composite, the presence of g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> prevents leaching of the polysulfides but <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XPS indicates transformation of CuS to Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S. The enhanced reversible capacity observed in the composite is attributed to the prevention of polysulfide leaching and formation of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S <span class="italic">via</span> addition of Cu in the anode from the Cu current collector. Finally, a sodium ion full cell with NVP cathode and 0.8CuS:0.2g-C<small><sub>3</sub></small>N<small><sub>4</sub></small> anode has been constructed which yields a capacity of 266 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after a run of 100 cycles.</span>

<h2 id="sect1377"><span class="a_heading">Conflicts of interest</span></h2>
<span>There are no conflicts of interest to declare.</span>

They are usually only set in response to actions made by you which amount to a request for services, such as setting your privacy preferences, logging in or filling in forms. You can set your browser to block or alert you about these cookies, but some parts of the site will not then work. These cookies do not store any personally identifiable information.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0002"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0002">Analytical cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0002" id="ot-group-id-C0002" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0002"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Analytical cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0002">These cookies allow us to count visits and traffic sources so we can measure and improve the performance of our site. They help us to know which pages are the most and least popular and see how visitors move around the site. All information these cookies collect is aggregated and therefore anonymous. If you do not allow these cookies we will not know when you have visited our site, and will not be able to monitor its performance.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0003"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0003">Functional cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0003" id="ot-group-id-C0003" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0003"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Functional cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0003">These cookies enable the website to provide enhanced functionality and personalisation.
